       Disputed territory in the South Caucasus
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For the general history and geography of this disputed area, see <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Artsakh (disambiguation)">Artsakh</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "NKR" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/NKR_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="NKR (disambiguation)">NKR (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Artsakh</b>, officially the <b>Republic of Artsakh</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/ɑːr/: 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/x/: 'ch' in 'loch'">x</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Արցախի Հանրապետություն</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Armenian" title="Romanization of Armenian">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="hy-Latn" title="Armenian-language romanization">Artsakhi Hanrapetutyun</i>) or the <b>Nagorno-Karabakh Republic</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">Нагорно-Карабахская Республика</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language romanization">Nagorno-Karabakhskaya Respublika</i>, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Լեռնային Ղարաբաղ Հանրապետություն</span>),<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-5">[5]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">breakaway state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">South Caucasus</a> supported by <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, whose territory is internationally recognized as part of <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>. Artsakh controls part of the former <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a>, including the capital of <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. It is an <a href="/wiki/Enclave_and_exclave" title="Enclave and exclave">enclave</a> within Azerbaijan. Its only overland access route to Armenia is via the 5&nbsp;km (3.1&nbsp;mi) wide <a href="/wiki/Lachin_corridor" title="Lachin corridor">Lachin corridor</a> which is under the control of Russian peacekeepers. </p>
      <p>The predominantly Armenian-populated region of <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> was claimed by both the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a> when both countries became independent in 1918 after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, and a brief war over the region broke out in 1920. The dispute was largely shelved after the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> established control over the area, and created the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> (NKAO) within the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijan SSR</a> in 1923. During the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">fall of the Soviet Union</a>, the region re-emerged as a source of dispute between Armenia and Azerbaijan. In 1991, a <a href="/wiki/1991_Nagorno-Karabakh_independence_referendum" title="1991 Nagorno-Karabakh independence referendum">referendum</a> held in the NKAO and the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Shahumyan_Province" title="Shahumyan Province">Shahumyan Province</a> resulted in a declaration of independence. Ethnic conflict led to the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">1991–1994 Nagorno-Karabakh War</a>. Conflict has sporadically broken out since then, most significantly in the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war</a>. </p>
      <p>Artsakh is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Nagorno-Karabakh">legislature</a>. The country is reliant on and closely integrated with Armenia, in many ways functioning de facto as part of Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cornell_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cornell-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country is very mountainous, averaging 1,100 metres (3,600&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Metres_above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Metres above sea level">above sea level</a>. The population is 99.7% <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">ethnic Armenian</a>, and the primary spoken language is the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian language</a>. The population is overwhelmingly Christian, most being affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>. Several historical monasteries are popular with tourists, mostly from the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>, as most travel can take place only between Armenia and Artsakh. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D4%B1%D6%80%D6%81%D5%A1%D5%AD" class="extiw" title="wikt:Արցախ">Արցախ</a> in Wiktionary for more.
      </div> 
      <p>According to scholars, inscriptions dating to the <a href="/wiki/Urartian_language" title="Urartian language">Urartian</a> period mention the region under a variety of names: "Ardakh", "Urdekhe", and "Atakhuni".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ASE_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASE-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In his <i><a href="/wiki/Geography_(Strabo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Geography (Strabo)">Geography</a></i>, the classical historian <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a> refers to an Armenian region which he calls "Orchistene", which is believed by some to be a <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> version of the old name of Artsakh.<sup id="cite_ref-Strabo_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Strabo-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to another hypothesis put forth by <a href="/wiki/David_M._Lang" class="mw-redirect" title="David M. Lang">David M. Lang</a>, the ancient name of Artsakh possibly derives from the name of King <a href="/wiki/Artaxias_I" title="Artaxias I">Artaxias I</a> of Armenia (190–159 BC), founder of the <a href="/wiki/Artaxiad_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Artaxiad Dynasty">Artaxiad Dynasty</a> and the kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(Antiquity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Armenia (Antiquity)">Greater Armenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">Folk etymology</a> holds that the name is derived from "Ar" (Aran) and "tsakh" (woods, garden) (i.e., the gardens of Aran Sisakean, the first <a href="/wiki/Nakharar" title="Nakharar">nakharar</a> of northeastern Armenia).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The name "Nagorno-Karabakh", commonly used in English, comes from the Russian name which means "Mountainous Karabakh". Karabakh is a Turkish/Persian word thought to mean "black garden". The Azerbaijani name for the area, "Dağlıq Qarabağ", has the same meaning as the Russian name. The term "Artsakh" lacks the non-Armenian influences present in "Nagorno-Karabakh". It was revived for use in the 19th century, and is the preferred term used by the locals, in English and Russian as well as Armenian.<sup id="cite_ref-Toal_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toal-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Artsakh" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Artsakh">History of Artsakh</a>
      </div>
      <table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Artsakh&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22">"Republic of Artsakh"</a>&nbsp;–&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22">scholar</a>&nbsp;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Republic+of+Artsakh%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2020</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The earliest record of the region covered by modern-day Artsakh is from <a href="/wiki/Urartu" title="Urartu">Urartian</a> inscriptions referring to the region as <i>Urtekhini</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It is unclear if the region was ever ruled by Urartu, but it was in close proximity to other Urartian domains. It may have been inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Caspians" title="Caspians">Caspian tribes</a> and/or by <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>. </p>
      <p>After decades of raids by the <a href="/wiki/Cimmerians" title="Cimmerians">Cimmerians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Medes</a>, Urartu finally collapsed with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Medes" title="Medes">Median Empire</a>, and shortly after, the geopolitical region previously ruled as Urartu re-emerged as <a href="/wiki/Satrapy_of_Armenia" title="Satrapy of Armenia">Armenia</a>. By the 5th century BC, Artsakh was part of Armenia under the <a href="/wiki/Orontid_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Orontid Dynasty">Orontid Dynasty</a>. It continued to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Artaxiad_dynasty" title="Artaxiad dynasty">Artaxiad Dynasty</a>, under which Armenia became one of the largest realms in <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>. At its greatest extent, the <a href="/wiki/Great_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Great King">Great King</a> of Armenia, <a href="/wiki/Tigranes_the_Great" title="Tigranes the Great">Tigranes II</a>, built several cities named after himself in regions he considered particularly important, one of which was the <a href="/wiki/Tigranakert_of_Artsakh" title="Tigranakert of Artsakh">city</a> he built in <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_(historic_province)" title="Artsakh (historic province)">Artsakh</a>. </p>
      <p>Following wars with the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Persians</a>, Armenia was partitioned between the two empires. Artsakh was removed from <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Armenia" title="Sasanian Armenia">Persian Armenia</a> and included into the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Satrap" title="Satrap">satrapy</a> of <a href="/wiki/Albania_(satrapy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Albania (satrapy)">Arran</a>. At this time, the population of Artsakh consisted of <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a> and <i>Armenicized</i> aborigines, though many of the latter were still cited as distinct ethnic entities.<sup id="cite_ref-Hewsen_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hewsen-18">[18]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_dialect" title="Karabakh dialect">dialect of Armenian</a> spoken in Artsakh was among the earliest ever recorded dialects of <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> which was described around this time in the 7th century AD by a contemporary named Stephanos Siunetzi.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (October 2020)">better&nbsp;source&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Arcax.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Arcax.jpg/260px-Arcax.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Arcax.jpg/390px-Arcax.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Arcax.jpg/520px-Arcax.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1680" data-file-height="1196"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Arcax.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The lands of <a href="/wiki/Syunik_(historic_province)" title="Syunik (historic province)">Syunik</a> (left) and Artsakh (right) until the early 9th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Artsakh remained part of Arran throughout Persian rule, during the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Persia" title="Muslim conquest of Persia">fall of Iran to the Muslims</a>, and following the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Armenia" title="Muslim conquest of Armenia">Muslim conquest of Armenia</a>. Under the Arabs, most of the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">South Caucasus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Highlands" title="Armenian Highlands">Armenian Highlands</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Iberia" title="Principality of Iberia">Iberia</a> and Arran, were unified into an <a href="/wiki/Emirate" title="Emirate">emirate</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Arminiya" title="Arminiya">Arminiya</a></i>, under which Artsakh continued to remain as part of Arran. </p>
      <p>Despite being under Persian and Arab rule, many of the Armenian territories, including Artsakh, were governed by Armenian nobility. Arran gradually disappeared as a geopolitical entity, while its population was assimilated by neighbouring ethnic groups with whom they shared a common culture and religion. Many Christians from Arran would <a href="/wiki/Ethnogenesis" title="Ethnogenesis">form part of the ethnic composition</a> of the Armenians living in modern-day Artsakh.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fragmentation of Arab authority provided the opportunity for the resurgence of an Armenian state in the Armenian Highlands. One particular noble dynasty, the <a href="/wiki/Bagratid_dynasty_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bagratid dynasty of Armenia">Bagratids</a>, began annexing territories from other Armenian nobles, which, in the latter half of the 9th century gave rise to a new <a href="/wiki/Bagratid_Armenia" title="Bagratid Armenia">Armenian kingdom</a> which included Artsakh. </p>
      <p>The new Kingdom didn't stay united for long, however, due to internal conflicts, civil wars, and external pressures, Armenia often found itself fragmented between other noble Armenian houses, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Mamikonian" title="Mamikonian">Mamikonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siunia_dynasty" title="Siunia dynasty">Siunia</a> families, the latter of which would produce a <a href="/wiki/Cadet_branch" title="Cadet branch">cadet branch</a> known as the House of Khachen, named after their stronghold in Artsakh. The House of Khachen ruled the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Artsakh" title="Kingdom of Artsakh">Kingdom of Artsakh</a> in the 11th century as an independent kingdom under the protectorate of the Bagratid Kingdom of Armenia. Under the House of Khachen, the region historically called Artsakh became synonymous with the name "Khachen". </p>
      <p>Following wars with the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, and with the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Turks</a> in the latter half of the 11th century, the Kingdom of Armenia collapsed, and Artsakh became the autonomous <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Khachen" title="Principality of Khachen">Principality of Khachen</a>, ruled by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hasan-Jalalyan" title="House of Hasan-Jalalyan">House of Hasan-Jalalyan</a>, within the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Georgia" title="Kingdom of Georgia">Kingdom of Georgia</a> for a short time until the <a href="/wiki/Ilkhanate" title="Ilkhanate">Mongols</a> acquired the region. Although the Armenians of Artsakh did not rule the lands as fully sovereign entities, the mountainous geography of the location allowed them to maintain a semi-independent or autonomous status within other realms, such as the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_Empire" title="Timurid Empire">Timurid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kara_Koyunlu" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara Koyunlu">Kara Koyunlu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aq_Qoyunlu" title="Aq Qoyunlu">Ak Koyunlu</a> realms. </p>
      <p>During this time, the lands to the west of the <a href="/wiki/Kura_(Caspian_Sea)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kura (Caspian Sea)">Kura river</a> up to the eastern slopes of the <a href="/wiki/Zangezur_Mountains" title="Zangezur Mountains">Zangezur mountain range</a> became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Karabakh" title="Karabakh">Karabakh</a></i>, with the lands of the Principality of Khachen corresponding to the highlands. During the period of Mongol domination, a great number of Armenians left the lowlands of Karabakh and sought refuge in the mountainous heights of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Principality of Khachen was eventually divided amongst five Armenian princes, known as meliks, who collectively became known as the <a href="/wiki/Melikdoms_of_Karabakh" title="Melikdoms of Karabakh">Five Melikdoms of Karabakh</a> (literally "five principalities of Karabakh"; also referred to as <i>Khamsa</i>, meaning "five" in Arabic). </p>
      <p>In the 16th century, Karabakh came under Iranian rule for the first time in almost a millennium with the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Safavid_dynasty" title="Safavid dynasty">Safavid Empire</a>, within which the territory of modern-day Artsakh became part of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Province of Karabakh">Province of Karabakh</a>. The Armenian princes continued to rule autonomously over the highlands of Karabakh during this time. </p>
      <p>In the mid-18th century, the whole of Karabakh became a semi-independent <a href="/wiki/Khanates_of_the_Caucasus" title="Khanates of the Caucasus">khanate</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Karabakh_Khanate" title="Karabakh Khanate">Karabakh Khanate</a> which lasted for about 75 years. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> advanced into the region in 1805, declared Artsakh a Russian protectorate and formally annexed it from <a href="/wiki/Qajar_Iran" title="Qajar Iran">Iran</a> in 1813 according to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Gulistan" title="Treaty of Gulistan">Treaty of Gulistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The Armenian princes lost their status as princes (<i>meliks</i>) in 1822. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg/220px-Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg/330px-Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg/440px-Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8925" data-file-height="6640"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karte_des_Kaukasischen_Isthmus_-_Entworfen_und_gezeichnet_von_J-Grassl_-_1856.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>An 1856 German-language map labelling the region "Artssakh"
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Following the collapse of the Russian Empire during World War I, <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> became the stage of wars between every political entity that emerged in the region (<a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Georgia" title="Democratic Republic of Georgia">Georgia</a>) and their neighbours (<a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>). The newly formed <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">Republic of Armenia</a> (declared on 28 May 1918) claimed most of the highlands of <a href="/wiki/Karabakh" title="Karabakh">Karabakh</a>, which was also claimed by the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a>. Assistance from the Republic of Armenia to Karabakh was limited as it found itself fighting enemies on all fronts, but the Armenian irregulars in Zangezur and the territories formerly known as Khachen (Artsakh) managed to maintain their control over the lands, consistently fighting off offensives from Azerbaijan and quelling Muslim uprisings from within. Azerbaijan maintained control of the lowlands of Karabakh and some regions between Zangezur and Artsakh. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire">Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire</span></h3> 
      <p>In 1918, the predominantly Armenian-populated region of <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> was claimed by both the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Democratic_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Democratic Republic">Azerbaijan Democratic Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">First Republic of Armenia</a> when both countries became independent after the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, and a brief war over the region broke out in 1920. The dispute was largely shelved after the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> established control over the area, and created the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> (NKAO) within the <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Azerbaijani SSR</a> in 1923. During the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">fall of the Soviet Union</a>, the region re-emerged as a source of dispute between Armenia and Azerbaijan. In 1991, a <a href="/wiki/1991_Nagorno-Karabakh_independence_referendum" title="1991 Nagorno-Karabakh independence referendum">referendum</a> held in the NKAO and the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Shahumian" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahumian">Shahumian</a> region resulted in a declaration of independence. The ethnic conflict led to the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">1991–1994 Nagorno-Karabakh War</a>, which ended with a ceasefire along roughly the current borders. According to <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHCR">UNHCR</a>, the conflict resulted in over 600,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> within <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the collapse of the Ottoman Empire, the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> established itself in Azerbaijan, and advocated that all of Karabakh (including Zangezur and Artsakh) should be part of Azerbaijan until the boundaries can be decided upon peacefully at the upcoming <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference of 1919</a>, but the battles did not cease until the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> from <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russia</a> began reclaiming the former territories of the Russian Empire and created <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Azerbaijan</a> out of the Azerbaijan Democratic Republic in 1920. The Armenians of Zangezur and Artsakh had consistently maintained control of the region and intended to unite with Armenia during the entirety of the two years of chaos, with Azerbaijan only temporarily occupying parts of the regions at certain times. The fall of Azerbaijan gave Armenia the opportunity to properly unite with the Armenian irregulars in Zangezur and Artsakh, but they were taken by the Red Army on 26 May 1920. The rest of Armenia fell to the Red Army shortly after. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> tried to end the centuries-long rivalry between Russia and Turkey, and in 1921, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a> formally transferred the Armenian-populated highlands of Karabakh to <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Azerbaijan Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Azerbaijan</a> to try to placate Turkey,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> though the majority of Zangezur remained within <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Armenian Soviet Socialist Republic">Soviet Armenia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In December 1920 under Soviet pressure central authorities issued a statement that Karabakh, Zangezur and Nakhjivan were all transferred to Armenian control. Stalin (then commissar for nationalities) made the decision public on 2 December, but the Azerbaijani leader Narimanov later denied the transfer.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under these circumstances, Soviet Armenia and Soviet Azerbaijan were admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> on 20 December 1922. The inclusion of Artsakh within Soviet Azerbaijan caused an uproar amongst Armenians, which led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> within Soviet Azerbaijan on 7 July 1923 (implemented in November 1924). Although the Armenians in Nagorno-Karabakh continued to desire reunification with Armenia, the conflict was largely dormant during the Soviet era.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Soviet_era">Post-Soviet era</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">First Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict" title="Nagorno-Karabakh conflict">Nagorno-Karabakh conflict</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg/220px-Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg/330px-Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg/440px-Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1292" data-file-height="1423"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_Republic_1994-2020.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Artsakh and surrounding territories. The area surrounded by red borders corresponds to territory de facto controlled by the Republic of Artsakh from 1994 until 2020. Yellow regions correspond to the Soviet-era Nagorno Karabakh Autonomous Oblast (NKAO), with yellow striped regions controlled by Azerbaijan but claimed by the Republic of Artsakh. Green striped regions correspond to territories outside the former NKAO held by Artsakh until the end of the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a>, the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict was revitalized. The Armenians of <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> declared their independence as the <i>Republic of Mountainous Karabakh</i> with the intention of reunifying with the newly independent <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>. The declaration was rejected by the newly independent <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, leading to the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">Nagorno-Karabakh War</a> from 20 February 1988 to 12 May 1994, resulting in a ceasefire in May 1994<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and the de facto independence of the Republic of Artsakh, whose territory remains internationally recognized as part of the Republic of Azerbaijan. </p>
      <p>Intermittent fighting over the region continued after the 1994 ceasefire without significant territorial changes,<sup id="cite_ref-diplomatie_150720_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-diplomatie_150720-28">[28]</a></sup> while long-standing international mediation attempts to create a peace process were initiated by the <a href="/wiki/OSCE_Minsk_Group" title="OSCE Minsk Group">OSCE Minsk Group</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MinskGroup_2Oct2020_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MinskGroup_2Oct2020-31">[31]</a></sup> From late September 2020 until November, <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">significant fighting resumed</a> and Azerbaijan recaptured territories, primarily in the southern part of the region. A <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_ceasefire_agreement" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement">peace deal</a> signed on 10 November 2020 between Armenia, Azerbaijan and Russia declared an end to the renewed fighting, and established that Armenia would withdraw from remaining occupied territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh over the next month. The deal includes provisions for a Russian peacekeeping force to deploy to the region, with Russian President Vladimir Putin stating that he intends for the current agreement to "create the conditions for a long-term settlement"<sup id="cite_ref-:2_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Artsakh" title="Politics of Artsakh">Politics of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:NKR_Parliament,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/220px-NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/330px-NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/440px-NKR_Parliament%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="875"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:NKR_Parliament,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The National Assembly of Artsakh in Stepanakert
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Artsakh is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> (in the middle of transforming from a semi-presidential one, after the <a href="/wiki/2017_Nagorno-Karabakh_constitutional_referendum" title="2017 Nagorno-Karabakh constitutional referendum">2017 referendum</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">Prime Minister</a>'s post was abolished and the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> is now residing with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">President</a> who is both the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The president is directly elected for a maximum of two-consecutive five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-5">[5]</a></sup> The current President is <a href="/wiki/Arayik_Harutyunyan" title="Arayik Harutyunyan">Arayik Harutyunyan</a> who was sworn in on 21 May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Nagorno-Karabakh">National Assembly</a> is a unicameral legislature. It has 33 members who are elected for 5-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-National_assembly_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-National_assembly-34">[34]</a></sup> Elections take place within a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>; in 2009, the American NGO <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> ranked the Republic of Artsakh above the republics of <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Armenia" title="Politics of Armenia">Armenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Azerbaijan" title="Politics of Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> with respect to <a href="/wiki/Civil_and_political_rights" title="Civil and political rights">civil and political rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Five parties have members in the parliament: the <a href="/wiki/Free_Motherland" title="Free Motherland">Free Motherland</a> party has 15 members, <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Revolutionary_Federation" title="Armenian Revolutionary Federation">ARF</a> has 8 members, <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Artsakh" title="Democratic Party of Artsakh">Democratic Party of Artsakh</a> has 7 members, <a href="/wiki/Movement_88" title="Movement 88">Movement 88</a> has 2 members and the <a href="/wiki/National_Revival_(Artsakh)" title="National Revival (Artsakh)">National Revival</a> party has one member. A number of non-partisan candidates have also taken part in the <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in Nagorno-Karabakh">elections</a>, with some success; in 2015, two of the 33 members to the National Assembly took their seats without running under the banner of any of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="List of political parties in Nagorno-Karabakh">established political parties</a> in the republic. Elections in Artsakh are not recognised by international bodies such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, as well as numerous individual countries, who called them a source of increased tensions.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Artsakh is heavily dependent on Armenia, and in many ways <i>de facto</i> functions and is administered as part of Armenia. However, Armenia is hesitant to officially recognise Artsakh.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cornell_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cornell-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Artsakh" title="Constitution of Artsakh">Constitution of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential,_NKR,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/220px-Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/330px-Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/440px-Presidential%2C_NKR%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1160" data-file-height="870"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential,_NKR,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Presidential Palace
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_(Artsakh)_46.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg/220px-2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg/330px-2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg/440px-2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_%28Artsakh%29_46.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017-07-26_-_Stepanakert_(Artsakh)_46.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The government building
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The founding documents of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic were the <i>Proclamation of the Nagorno Karabakh Republic</i> and the <i>Declaration of State Independence of the Nagorno Karabakh Republic</i>. For a long time no constitution was created, with the republic instead declaring Armenian law applied on its territory through a 1992 law. Even when new laws were passed, they were often copies of equivalent Armenian laws.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 3 November 2006, the then-President of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic, <a href="/wiki/Arkadi_Ghukasyan" title="Arkadi Ghukasyan">Arkadi Ghukasyan</a>, signed a decree to hold <a href="/wiki/2006_Nagorno-Karabakh_constitutional_referendum" title="2006 Nagorno-Karabakh constitutional referendum">a referendum</a> on a draft Nagorno-Karabakh constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> It was held on 10 December of the same year and according to official preliminary results, with a turnout of 87.2%,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> as many as 98.6 percent of voters approved the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-RFE_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE-43">[43]</a></sup> The first article of the document described the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic, alternatively called the Republic of Artsakh, as "a sovereign, democratic state based on social justice and the rule of law."<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_2016_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution_2016-45">[45]</a></sup> More than 100 non-governmental international observers and journalists who monitored the poll evaluated it positively, stating that it was held to a high international standard.<sup id="cite_ref-IWPR_-_Constitution_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IWPR_-_Constitution-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, the vote was criticised harshly by inter-governmental organisations such as the European Union, <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> and <a href="/wiki/GUAM" class="mw-redirect" title="GUAM">GUAM</a>, which rejected the referendum, deeming it illegitimate.<sup id="cite_ref-IWPR_-_Constitution_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IWPR_-_Constitution-46">[46]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The EU announced it was "aware that a 'constitutional referendum' has taken place," but emphasised its stance that only a negotiated settlement between Azerbaijan and ethnic Armenians could bring a lasting solution.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Secretary_General_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Secretary General of the Council of Europe">Secretary General of the Council of Europe</a> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Davis_(politician)" title="Terry Davis (politician)">Terry Davis</a> asserted that the poll "will not be recognized... and is therefore of no consequence".<sup id="cite_ref-IWPR_-_Constitution_46-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IWPR_-_Constitution-46">[46]</a></sup> In a statement, the OSCE chairman in office <a href="/wiki/Karel_De_Gucht" title="Karel De Gucht">Karel De Gucht</a> voiced his concern that the vote would prove harmful to the ongoing conflict settlement process, which, he said, had shown "visible progress" and was at a "promising juncture".<sup id="cite_ref-RFE_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The holding of the referendum was also criticised by Turkey, which traditionally supports Azerbaijan because of common ethnic Turkic roots, and has historically had <a href="/wiki/Armenia-Turkey_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Armenia-Turkey relations">severe tensions</a> with Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/2017_Nagorno-Karabakh_constitutional_referendum" title="2017 Nagorno-Karabakh constitutional referendum">Another referendum</a> was held on 20 February 2017, with an 87.6% vote in favour on a 76% turnout for instituting a new constitution. This constitution among other changes turned the government from a semi-presidential to a fully presidential model. Its name was changed from "Constitution of the Nagorno Karabakh Republic" to "Constitution of the Republic of Artsakh", though both remained official names of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-armenian-weekly-2017-02-21_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-armenian-weekly-2017-02-21-52">[52]</a></sup> The new name implies a claim to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian-occupied_territories_surrounding_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Armenian-occupied territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh">areas occupied</a> beyond the former <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and the Presidential system allows for quicker decisions on security matters. The referendum is seen as a response to the <a href="/wiki/2016_Nagorno-Karabakh_clashes" class="mw-redirect" title="2016 Nagorno-Karabakh clashes">2016 Nagorno-Karabakh clashes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Artsakh" title="Foreign relations of Artsakh">Foreign relations of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg/220px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg/330px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg/440px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_%2802%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Budynek_Ministerstwa_Spraw_Zagranicznych_Republiki_G%C3%B3rskiego_Karabachu_(02).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Artsakh in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is based in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. Since no UN member or observer currently recognizes Artsakh, none of its foreign relations are of an official diplomatic nature. However, the Republic of Artsakh operates five permanent Missions and one Bureau of Social-Politic Information in France. Artsakh's Permanent Missions exist in <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>, Australia, France, Germany, Russia, the United States, and one for Middle East countries based in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> The goals of the offices are to present the Republic's positions on various issues, to provide information and to facilitate the peace process. </p>
      <p>In his 2015 speech, the President of Armenia <a href="/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan" title="Serzh Sargsyan">Serzh Sargsyan</a> stated that he considered Nagorno-Karabakh "an inseparable part of Armenia".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Republic of Artsakh is neither a member nor observer of the UN or any of its specialized agencies. However, it is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Community_for_Democracy_and_Rights_of_Nations" title="Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations">Community for Democracy and Rights of Nations</a>, commonly known as the "Commonwealth of Unrecognized States", and is recognized by <a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_Defence_Army" title="Artsakh Defence Army">Artsakh Defence Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">First Nagorno-Karabakh War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG/220px-Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG/330px-Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG/440px-Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_Graveyard.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The graves of Armenian soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the Constitution of Artsakh, the army is under the civilian command of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_Defense_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Artsakh Defense Army">Artsakh Defense Army</a> was officially established on 9 May 1992 as a defense against Azerbaijan. It fought the Azerbaijani army to a ceasefire on 12 May 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Currently the Artsakh Defense Army consists of around 18,000–20,000 officers and soldiers. However, only 8,500 citizens from Artsakh serve in the Artsakh army; some 10,000 come from Armenia. There are also 177–316 <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a>, 256–324 additional fighting vehicles, and 291–322 guns and <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">mortars</a>. Armenia supplies arms and other military necessities to Artsakh. Several battalions of Armenia's army are deployed directly in the Artsakh zone on occupied Azerbaijani territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Blandy_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blandy-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Artsakh Defense Army <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Shusha" class="mw-redirect" title="Capture of Shusha">fought in Shusha</a> in 1992, opening the <a href="/wiki/Lachin_corridor" title="Lachin corridor">Lachin corridor</a> between Armenia and Nagorno-Karabakh (1992), and staged the defence of the <a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a> front from 1992 to 1994. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_mines">Land mines</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Land_mine_situation_in_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Land mine situation in Nagorno-Karabakh">Land mine situation in Nagorno-Karabakh</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Mines were laid in the region from 1991 to 1994 by both conflicting parties in the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">first Nagorno-Karabakh War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Program</a> (UNDP) claims that 123 people have been killed and over 300 injured by landmines near the disputed enclave of Nagorno-Karabakh since a 1994 truce ended a six-year conflict between ethnic Armenian and Azerbaijani forces.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/HALO_Trust" title="HALO Trust">HALO Trust</a>, a UK-based demining NGO, is the only international organisation conducting <a href="/wiki/Demining" title="Demining">demining</a> in Nagorno Karabakh.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> They have destroyed 180,858 small arms ammunition, 48,572 units of "other explosive items", 12,423 cluster bombs, 8,733 anti-personnel landmines, and 2,584 anti-tank landmines between 2000 and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> By 2018, they had cleared 88% of the territory's minefields, with a target to clear the rest by 2020. The main cities of <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shusha" title="Shusha">Shusha</a>, as well as the main north–south highway, have been cleared and are safe for travel. The demining effort has been largely funded by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">United States Agency for International Development</a> (USAID).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_situation">Current situation</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Artsakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Political status of Artsakh">Political status of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <img alt="Ambox current red Americas.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290">
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section needs to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2020</span>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>Today, Artsakh is a <i>de facto</i> <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">independent</a> state, calling itself the <i>Republic of Artsakh</i>. It has close relations with <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> and uses the same currency, the <a href="/wiki/Dram_(currency)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dram (currency)">dram</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, "from the beginning of the Karabakh conflict, Armenia provided aid, weapons, and volunteers. Armenian involvement in Artsakh escalated after a December 1993 Azerbaijani offensive. The Republic of Armenia began sending conscripts and regular Army and Interior Ministry troops to fight in Artsakh."<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The politics of Armenia and the de facto Artsakh are so intertwined that <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kocharyan" title="Robert Kocharyan">Robert Kocharyan</a> served as the first President of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic, from 1994 to 1997, then as prime minister of Armenia from 1997 to 1998, and then as the second President of Armenia, from 1998 to 2008. </p>
      <p>However, Armenian governments have repeatedly resisted internal pressure to unite the two, due to ongoing negotiations under the auspices of the <a href="/wiki/OSCE_Minsk_Group" title="OSCE Minsk Group">OSCE Minsk Group</a>. In his case study of Eurasia, Dov Lynch of the Institute for Security Studies of <a href="/wiki/WEU" class="mw-redirect" title="WEU">WEU</a> believes that "Karabakh's independence allows the new Armenian state to avoid the international stigma of aggression, despite the fact that Armenian troops fought in the war between 1991–94 and continue to man the Line of Contact between Karabakh and Azerbaijan." Lynch also cites that the "strength of the Armenian armed forces, and Armenia's strategic alliance with Russia, are seen as key shields protecting the Karabakh state by the authorities in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Some sources consider Artsakh as functioning <i>de facto</i> as a part of Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hurriyetdailynews1_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurriyetdailynews1-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg/220px-Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg/330px-Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg/440px-Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3640" data-file-height="2517"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_June_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>General view of the capital <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At present, the mediation process is at a standstill, with the most recent discussions in <a href="/wiki/Rambouillet" title="Rambouillet">Rambouillet</a>, France, yielding no agreement. Azerbaijan has officially requested Armenian troops to withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Security_belt_of_Nagorno-Karabakh_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Security belt of Nagorno-Karabakh Republic">all disputed areas of Azerbaijan outside Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, and that all displaced persons be allowed to return to their homes before the status of Karabakh can be discussed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Armenia does not recognise Azerbaijani claims to Nagorno-Karabakh and believes the territory should have self-determination.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Both the Armenian and Artsakhi governments note that the independence of Artsakh was declared around the time the Soviet Union dissolved and its members became independent.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The Armenian government insists that the government of Artsakh be part of any discussions on the region's future, and rejects ceding occupied territory or allowing refugees to return before talks on the region's status.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Representatives of Armenia, Azerbaijan, France, Russia and the United States met in Paris and in <a href="/wiki/Key_West" title="Key West">Key West</a>, Florida, in early 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-state2001_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state2001-74">[74]</a></sup> Despite rumours that the parties were close to a solution, the Azerbaijani authorities&nbsp;– both during <a href="/wiki/Heydar_Aliyev" title="Heydar Aliyev">Heydar Aliyev</a>'s period of office, and after the accession of his son <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a> in the October 2003 elections&nbsp;– have firmly denied that any agreement was reached in Paris or Key West. </p>
      <p>Further talks between the Azerbaijani and Armenian presidents, <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kocharyan" title="Robert Kocharyan">Robert Kocharyan</a>, were held in September 2004 in Astana, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, on the sidelines of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> (CIS) summit. Reportedly, one of the suggestions put forward was the withdrawal of the occupying forces from the Azeri territories adjacent to Artsakh and then holding <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendums</a> (plebiscites) in Artsakh and Azerbaijan proper regarding the future status of the region. On 10 and 11 February 2006, Kocharyan and Aliyev met in <a href="/wiki/Rambouillet" title="Rambouillet">Rambouillet</a>, France, to discuss the fundamental principles of a settlement to the conflict. Contrary to the initial optimism, the Rambouillet talks did not produce any agreement, with key issues such as the status of Artsakh and whether Armenian troops would withdraw from <a href="/wiki/Kalbajar" title="Kalbajar">Kalbajar</a> still being contentious.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Talks were held at the Polish embassy in <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a> in June 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Again, American, Russian, and French diplomats attended the talks that lasted over 40 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Earlier, Armenian President Kocharyan announced that he was ready to "continue dialogue with Azerbaijan for the settlement of the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict and with Turkey on establishing relations without any preconditions".<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Chartar2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Chartar2.JPG/220px-Chartar2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Chartar2.JPG/330px-Chartar2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Chartar2.JPG/440px-Chartar2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Chartar2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The town of <a href="/wiki/Chartar_(town)" title="Chartar (town)">Chartar</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to Armenian foreign minister, <a href="/wiki/Vardan_Oskanyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Vardan Oskanyan">Vardan Oskanyan</a>, no progress was made at this latest meeting. Both presidents failed to reach a consensus on the issues from the earlier Rambouillet conference. He noted that the Kocharyan-Aliyev meeting was held in a normal atmosphere. "Nevertheless," he added, "the foreign ministers of the two countries are commissioned to continue talks over the settlement of the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict and try to find common points before the next meeting of the presidents."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The major disagreement between both sides at the Bucharest conference was the status of Artsakh. Azerbaijan's preferred solution would be to give Artsakh the "highest status of autonomy adopted in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Armenia, on the other hand, endorsed a popular vote by the inhabitants of Artsakh to decide their future, a position that was also taken by the<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (October 2013)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> international mediators.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> On 27 June, the Armenian foreign minister said both parties agreed to allow the residents of Artsakh to vote regarding the future status of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The Azerbaijani Ministry of Foreign Affairs officially refuted that statement.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> According to Azeri opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Isa_Gambar" title="Isa Gambar">Isa Gambar</a>, however, Azerbaijan did indeed agree to the referendum. Still, nothing official has confirmed this yet.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ongoing "Prague Process" overseen by the OSCE Minsk Group was brought into sharp relief in the summer of 2006 with a series of rare public revelations seemingly designed to jump-start the stalled negotiations. After the release in June of a paper outlining its position, which had until then been carefully guarded, U.S. State Department official <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Bryza" title="Matthew Bryza">Matthew Bryza</a> told <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Free Europe">Radio Free Europe</a> that the Minsk Group favoured a referendum in Karabakh that would determine its final status. The referendum, in the view of the OSCE, should take place not in Azerbaijan as a whole, but in Artsakh only. This was a blow to Azerbaijan, and despite talk that their government might eventually seek a more sympathetic forum for future negotiations, this has not yet happened.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_(02).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg/220px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg/330px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg/440px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_%2802%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2692"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Monument_My_i_Nasze_G%C3%B3ry_(02).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The "<a href="/wiki/We_Are_Our_Mountains" title="We Are Our Mountains">We Are Our Mountains</a>" monument is widely seen as a symbol of the self-proclaimed republic.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 10 December 2007 Azerbaijan's deputy foreign minister said Azerbaijan would be prepared to conduct anti-terrorist operations in Nagorno-Karabakh against alleged bases of the <a href="/wiki/Kurdistan_Workers%27_Party" title="Kurdistan Workers' Party">Kurdistan Workers' Party</a> (PKK).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Armenian Foreign Ministry Spokesperson Vladimir Karapetian previously rejected the allegations as "fabricated" and suggested the accusations of the PKK presence were a form of provocation.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Azerbaijani president <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">Ilham Aliyev</a> stated that "Nagorno-Karabakh will never be independent; the position is backed by international mediators as well; Armenia has to accept the reality" and that "in 1918, <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> was granted to the <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>. It was a great mistake. The <a href="/wiki/Erivan_khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Erivan khanate">khanate of Iravan</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Azeris" class="mw-redirect" title="Azeris">Azeri</a> territory, the Armenians were guests here".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On the other hand, in 2009, the president of the Nagorno-Karabakh Republic <a href="/wiki/Bako_Sahakyan" title="Bako Sahakyan">Bako Sahakyan</a> declared that "Artsakh will never be a part of Azerbaijan. Artsakh security should never be an article of commerce either. As to other issues, we are ready to discuss them with Azerbaijan.".<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In 2010 president of Republic of Armenia <a href="/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan" title="Serzh Sargsyan">Serzh Sargsyan</a> in his speech in the Chatham House of the British Royal Institute of International Affairs declared that "Karabakh was never a part of independent Azerbaijan: it was annexed to Azerbaijan by a decision of the Soviet Union party body. The people of Karabakh never put up with this decision, and upon the first opportunity, seceded from the Soviet Union fully in line with the laws of the Soviet Union and the applicable international law".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 14 March 2008, the United Nations General Assembly passed a <a href="/wiki/Non-binding_resolution" title="Non-binding resolution">non-binding resolution</a> by a vote of 39 to 7, with 100 abstentions, reaffirming Azerbaijan's territorial integrity, expressing support for that country's internationally recognised borders and demanding the immediate withdrawal of all Armenian forces from all occupied territories there. The resolution was supported mainly by members of the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a> (OIC) and <a href="/wiki/GUAM" class="mw-redirect" title="GUAM">GUAM</a>, Azerbaijan is a member in both groups, as well as other nations facing breakaway regions. The resolution was opposed by all three members of the <a href="/wiki/OSCE" class="mw-redirect" title="OSCE">OSCE</a> Minsk Group.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 20 May 2010, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> adopted a resolution "on the need for an EU strategy for the South Caucasus", which states that EU must pursue a strategy to promote stability, prosperity and conflict resolution in the South Caucasus.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The resolution "calls on the parties to intensify their peace talk efforts for the purpose of a settlement in the coming months, to show a more constructive attitude and to abandon preferences to perpetuate the status quo created by force and with no international legitimacy, creating in this way instability and prolonging the suffering of the war-affected populations; condemns the idea of a military solution and the heavy consequences of military force already used, and calls on both parties to avoid any further breaches of the 1994 ceasefire".
