The resolution also calls for the withdrawal of Armenian forces from all occupied territories of Azerbaijan, accompanied by the deployment of international forces to be organised with respect of the UN Charter in order to provide the necessary security guarantees in a period of transition, which will ensure the security of the population of Artsakh and allow the displaced persons to return to their homes and further conflicts caused by homelessness to be prevented; and states that the EU believes that the position according to which Artsakh includes all occupied Azerbaijani lands surrounding Artsakh should rapidly be abandoned. It also notes "that an interim status for Nagorno-Karabakh could offer a solution until the final status is determined and that it could create a transitional framework for peaceful coexistence and cooperation of Armenian and Azerbaijani populations in the region."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 26 June 2010, the presidents of the OSCE Minsk Group's Co-Chair countries, France, Russia, and United States made a joint statement, reaffirming their "commitment to support the leaders of Armenia and Azerbaijan as they finalize the Basic Principles for the peaceful settlement of the Nagorno-Karabakh conflict".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During his August 2019 visit to Stepanakert, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Armenia" title="Prime Minister of Armenia">Prime Minister of Armenia</a> <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a> presented the strategic development goals set for Armenia for the next three decades. He added that he made no special provision for Nagorno-Karabakh because "Artsakh is Armenia and there is no alternative".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Soon afterwards, Armenia's Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Zohrab_Mnatsakanyan" title="Zohrab Mnatsakanyan">Zohrab Mnatsakanyan</a> commented on Pashinyan's statement by saying he had "nothing to add" to Pashinyan's formulation of Armenia's position in the conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-markovic_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-markovic-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On September 27, 2020, <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh War">fighting broke out</a> between Armenia and Azerbaijan over Artsakh,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2020clashes_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2020clashes-98">[98]</a></sup> which may have claimed thousands of lives.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Azerbaijan recaptured territories, primarily in the southern part of the region. <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_ceasefire_agreement" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement">A ceasefire agreement</a> signed on 10 November 2020 between Armenia, Azerbaijan and Russia declared an end to the renewed fighting, and established that Armenia would withdraw from remaining occupied territories surrounding the former Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast over the next month, while maintaining control over the areas of the former oblast that had not been captured during the war. The deal includes provisions for a Russian peacekeeping force to deploy to the region, with Russian President Vladimir Putin stating that he intends for the current agreement to "create the conditions for a long-term settlement".<sup id="cite_ref-:2_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-32">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_St._Watertown,_MA.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG/220px-Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG/330px-Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG/440px-Artsakh_St._Watertown%2C_MA.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_St._Watertown,_MA.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Artsakh Street in <a href="/wiki/Watertown,_Massachusetts" title="Watertown, Massachusetts">Watertown, Massachusetts</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>No UN member states have recognised Artsakh,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> although some unrecognised and partially recognized states have done so.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Various sub-national governments have issued calls for recognition of Artsakh by their national governments.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2021, Russia, Azerbaijan, and Armenia held a trilateral meeting about Artsakh. This is expected to be the first of a regular series of meetings between the three countries, per an agreement to promote economic and infrastructure development throughout the region.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Displaced_people">Displaced people</span></h3> 
      <p>The Nagorno-Karabakh conflict has resulted in the displacement of 597,000 Azerbaijanis (this figure includes 230,000 children born to <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs) and 54,000 who have returned)<sup id="cite_ref-auto_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-103">[103]</a></sup> including Artsakh, and 220,000 Azeris, 18,000 Kurds and 3,500 Russians fled from Armenia to Azerbaijan from 1988 to 1989. The Azerbaijani government has estimated that 63% of IDPs lived below the poverty line as compared to 49% of the total population. About 154,000 lived in the capital, Baku. According to the International Organization for Migration, 40,000 IDPs lived in camps, 60,000 in dugout shelters, and 20,000 in railway cars. Forty-thousand IDPs lived in EU-funded settlements and UNHCR provided housing for another 40,000. Another 5,000 IDPs lived in abandoned or rapidly deteriorating schools. Others lived in trains, on roadsides in half-constructed buildings, or in public buildings such as tourist and health facilities. Tens of thousands lived in seven tent camps where poor water supply and sanitation caused gastrointestinal infections, tuberculosis, and malaria.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The government required IDPs to register their place of residence in an attempt to better target the limited and largely inadequate national and international assistance due to the Armenian advocated and US imposed restrictions on humanitarian aid to Azerbaijan. Many IDPs were from rural areas and found it difficult to integrate into the urban labor market. Many international humanitarian agencies reduced or ceased assistance for IDPs citing increasing oil revenues of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-wrs2005_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrs2005-105">[105]</a></sup> The infant mortality among displaced Azerbaijani children is 3–4 times higher than in the rest of the population. The rate of <a href="/wiki/Stillbirth" title="Stillbirth">stillbirth</a> was 88.2 per 1,000 births among the internally displaced people. The majority of the displaced have lived in difficult conditions for more than 13 years.<sup id="cite_ref-gidp_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gidp-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">2020 war</a> <a href="/wiki/Ilham_Aliyev" title="Ilham Aliyev">President Aliyev</a> stated he intends for refugees to return to the area.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> While many former cities are currently uninhabitable,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> the Azerbaijani government and some Azerbaijani companies have announced plans to rebuild infrastructure and invest in the newly controlled territories.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The Azerbaijani military is clearing mines prior to resettlement, which may take 10–13 years.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>280,000 persons—virtually all ethnic Armenians who fled Azerbaijan during the 1988–1993 war over the disputed region of Artsakh—were living in refugee-like circumstances in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-wrs2001_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrs2001-113">[113]</a></sup> Some left the country, principally to Russia. Their children born in Armenia acquire citizenship automatically. Their numbers are thus subject to constant decline due to departure, and de-registration required for naturalization. Of these, about 250,000 fled Azerbaijan (areas outside Nagorno-Karabakh); approximately 30,000 came from Nagorno-Karabakh. All were registered with the government as refugees at year's end.<sup id="cite_ref-wrs2001_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wrs2001-113">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <p>The Artsakh Republic is mountainous, a feature which has given it its former name (from the Russian for "Mountainous/Highland Karabakh"). It is 3,170&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,224&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) in area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The highest point in the country is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kirs" title="Mount Kirs">Mount Kirs</a> at 2,725 metres (8,940&nbsp;ft). The largest water body is the <a href="/wiki/Sarsang_reservoir" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarsang reservoir">Sarsang reservoir</a>, and the major rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Terter_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Terter river">Terter</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Khachen_river&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Khachen river (page does not exist)">Khachen</a> rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-114">[114]</a></sup> The country is on a plateau which slopes downwards towards the east and southeast, with the average altitude being 1,100&nbsp;m (3,600&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-115">[115]</a></sup> Most rivers in the country flow towards the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Artsakh_Valley&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Artsakh Valley (page does not exist)">Artsakh Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The climate is mild and temperate. The average temperature is 11&nbsp;°C (52&nbsp;°F), which fluctuates annually between 22&nbsp;°C (72&nbsp;°F) in July and −1&nbsp;°C (30&nbsp;°F) in January. The average precipitation can reach 710&nbsp;mm (28&nbsp;in) in some regions, and it is foggy for over 100 days a year.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-115">[115]</a></sup> Over 2,000 kinds of plants exist in Artsakh, and more than 36% of the country is forested. The plant life on the <a href="/wiki/Steppes" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppes">steppes</a> consists mostly of semi-desert vegetation, while <a href="/wiki/Subalpine_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Subalpine zone">subalpine zone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alpine_tundra" title="Alpine tundra">alpine tundra</a> ecosystems can be found above the forest in the highlands and mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-Geography_115-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geography-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_the_Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Administrative divisions of the Republic of Artsakh">Administrative divisions of the Republic of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Street_in_Martuni.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Street_in_Martuni.jpg/220px-Street_in_Martuni.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Street_in_Martuni.jpg/330px-Street_in_Martuni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Street_in_Martuni.jpg/440px-Street_in_Martuni.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

Horizontal dashed lines indicate territory under the control of Azerbaijan.)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of Artsakh currently claims seven administrative divisions. When established, Artsakh established eight administrative divisions, however, after the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_war" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war">2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kashatagh_Province" title="Kashatagh Province">Kashatagh Province</a> ceased to exist, as a claim no longer exists on this territory with the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_ceasefire_agreement" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh ceasefire agreement">per the ceasefire agreement</a> that ended the conflict. The territory of Artsakh includes most of four districts of the former <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> (NKAO), with the fifth district, <a href="/wiki/Hadrut_Province" title="Hadrut Province">Hadrut Province</a>, completely under Azerbaijani control. Also claimed by Artsakh is the <a href="/wiki/Shahumyan_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahumyan Region">Shahumyan Region</a> of the Azerbaijan SSR, which has been under Azerbaijani control since the <a href="/wiki/First_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" title="First Nagorno-Karabakh War">First Nagorno-Karabakh war</a>. While the Shahumyan Region was not part of the Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast, representatives from Shahumyan declared independence along with the Oblast, and the proclamation of Artsakh includes the Shahumyan region within its borders.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Prior to the 2020 war, the territory of Artsakh included most of the five districts of the former <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast">Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast</a> (NKAO), and parts of seven other former districts of the Azerbaijan SSR around the former NKAO that were under the control of Artsakhi forces.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Following the Republic of Artsakh's declaration of independence, the Azerbaijani government abolished the NKAO and created Azerbaijani districts in its place. As a result, some of Artsakh's divisions corresponded with the <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Azerbaijan" title="Administrative divisions of Azerbaijan">Azerbaijani districts</a>, while others had different borders. A comparative table of the established divisions of Artsakh and the corresponding districts of Azerbaijan follows:<sup id="cite_ref-azerbregions_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azerbregions-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Demographics of the Republic of Artsakh">Demographics of the Republic of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg/220px-Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg/330px-Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg/440px-Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tumo_Stepanakert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Children at <a href="/wiki/Tumo_Center_for_Creative_Technologies" title="Tumo Center for Creative Technologies">Tumo Center</a> Artsakh branch
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Azatamartikneri_boulevard,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/220px-Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/330px-Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg/440px-Azatamartikneri_boulevard%2C_Stepanakert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Azatamartikneri_boulevard,_Stepanakert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Freedom Fighters' Boulevard in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2002, the country's population was 145,000, made up of 95% Armenians and 5% others.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-114">[114]</a></sup> This composition represents a sharp change from the 1979 and 1989 census, when the Azerbaijani population was 23 and 21.5 percent, respectively. In March 2007, the local government announced that its population had grown to 138,000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The annual birth rate was recorded at 2,200–2,300 per year, an increase from nearly 1,500 in 1999. </p>
      <p>OSCE report, released in March 2011, estimates the population of the "seven occupied territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh" to be 14,000, and states "there has been no significant growth in the population since 2005."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> An <a href="/wiki/International_Crisis_Group" title="International Crisis Group">International Crisis Group</a> report published in December 2019 recorded the population of these territories to be 17,000, or 11.48% of the total population: 15,000 west and southwest of the former oblast, and 2000 in the <a href="/wiki/Agdam_District" title="Agdam District">Agdam District</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Until 2000, the country's net migration was at a negative.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> For the first half of 2007, 1,010 births and 659 deaths were reported, with a net emigration of 27.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to age group: 15,700 (0–6), 25,200 (7–17) 75,800 (18–59) and 21,000 (60+) </p>
      <p>Population by province (2006): </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a> 54,500 (2013)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Martuni_Province" title="Martuni Province">Martuni</a> 23,200</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a> 19,000</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Askeran_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Askeran Region">Askeran</a> 17,400 (2007)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Hadrut_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadrut Region">Hadrut</a> 12,300 (2009)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Qashatagh_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Qashatagh Province">Kashatagh</a> 9,800</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shushi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shushi">Shushi</a> 5,000 (2009)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Shahumyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahumyan">Shahumyan</a> 2,800</li>
      </ul>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_composition">Ethnic composition</span></h3>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Armenian_dialects" title="Armenian dialects">Armenian dialects</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_dialects" title="Russian dialects">Russian dialects</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The primary language spoken by the population 99.7% <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">ethnic Armenian</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian language</a>, which functions as the only state language and an official language in the Republic of Artsakh. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> is widely spoken in Arstakh and since late 2020-2021 efforts have been made in the parliament in Stepanakert to establish it as an additional official language; the official justifications for this being that Russian is already the second language of many residents, and that it "creates conditions for deepening cooperation in all spheres, and in the forseeable future will contribute to the development of relations within the legal framework."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> While Russian may soon get official status, Armenian will remain the only state language. The law recognises the state language as a "prevailing language in the republic" with "protection and sponsorship of the republic", and recognises the official language as that "which serves literary and scientific needs of the society", implicitly suggesting the utility of Russian in educational institutions and in science, but not necessarily in government procedures. <sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> There are some features to the variety of Russian as spoken in Arstakh, such as the use of <i>шпилька</i> in place of <i>прищепка</i> (clothespin), <i>пулпулак</i><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> for a waterfountain, and <i>финки</i> for sweatpants. <sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_towns">Cities and towns</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Artsakh" title="List of cities and towns in Artsakh">List of cities and towns in Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png/220px-Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png/330px-Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png/440px-Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png 2x" data-file-width="906" data-file-height="1209"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Republic_of_Artsakh_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Main cities and towns in Artsakh (territorial control shown is prior to the 2020 war)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The capital and by far largest city in Artsakh is Stepanakert (55,200 inhabitants in 2015), followed by <a href="/wiki/Martuni,_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Martuni, Nagorno-Karabakh">Martuni</a> (5,700), <a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a> (4,600), <a href="/wiki/Chartar_(town)" title="Chartar (town)">Chartar</a> (4,000), <a href="/wiki/Askeran" title="Askeran">Askeran</a> (2,300), <a href="/wiki/Lachin" title="Lachin">Berdzor</a> (1,900), <a href="/wiki/Haterk" title="Haterk">Haterk</a> (c. 1,600), <a href="/wiki/Karakend" title="Karakend">Berdashen</a> (c. 1,600), <a href="/wiki/Vank,_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Vank, Nagorno-Karabakh">Vank</a> (c. 1,600), <a href="/wiki/Noragyugh,_Azerbaijan" class="mw-redirect" title="Noragyugh, Azerbaijan">Noragyugh</a> (c. 1,500), <a href="/wiki/Khojaly_(town)" title="Khojaly (town)">Ivanyan</a> (c. 1,400), <a href="/wiki/Taghavard" title="Taghavard">Taghavard</a> (c. 1,300), <a href="/wiki/Gishi,_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Gishi, Nagorno-Karabakh">Gishi</a> (c. 1,100), <a href="/wiki/Q%C4%B1rm%C4%B1z%C4%B1_Bazar" title="Qırmızı Bazar">Karmir Shuka</a> (c. 1,100), <a href="/wiki/Sos,_Khojavend" class="mw-redirect" title="Sos, Khojavend">Sos</a> (c. 1,100), <a href="/wiki/Ball%C4%B1ca,_Khojaly" title="Ballıca, Khojaly">Aygestan</a> (c. 1,100) and <a href="/wiki/Xanabad,_Khojaly" title="Xanabad, Khojaly">Khnapat</a> (c. 1,000).<sup id="cite_ref-Census2015_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2015-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2015statistics_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015statistics-135">[135]</a></sup> This list only includes towns that remain in Artsakh after the 2020 war. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Resettlement_attempts_after_1994">Resettlement attempts after 1994</span></h3> 
      <p>While the territory captured outside the former NKAO was initially treated as a potential bargaining chip, it slowly began to be seen as part of the country by both officials and the general population.<sup id="cite_ref-Toal_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toal-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>-based administration launched various programs aimed at bringing in permanent Armenian settlers to the depopulated lands, including into regions previously populated by Azeris, with those that bordered Armenia – Lachin and Kalbajar – being the priority.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> Lachin was key to a land connection between Armenia and the former NKAO, and Kalbajar had water resources utilised by both Artsakh and Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-Toal_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toal-16">[16]</a></sup> Incentives in the form of free housing, access to property, social infrastructure, inexpensive or sometimes free electricity, running water, low taxes or limited tax exemptions were offered to new settlers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Azerbaijan regards this as a violation of Article 49 of the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Geneva_Convention" title="Fourth Geneva Convention">Fourth Geneva Convention</a>, to which Armenia became party in 1993, whereby "[t]he Occupying Power shall not deport or transfer parts of its own civilian population into the territory it occupies".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> The ruling party of Azerbaijan accuses the Armenian side of artificially changing the demographic situation and the ethnic composition of the occupied region so that it can lay future claims to them, comparing this to the 1950s campaign of resettling diaspora Armenians in previously Azeri-populated locales in Soviet Armenia where Azeris were forcibly <a href="/wiki/Deportation_of_Azerbaijanis_from_Armenia" title="Deportation of Azerbaijanis from Armenia">deported from in 1948–1950</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1979, the total Armenian population of the districts of Kalbajar, Lachin, Qubadli, Zangilan, Jabrayil, Fuzuli and Agdam was around 1,400 people.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> An OSCE fact-finding mission established at Azerbaijan's request visited these regions in February 2005 with the intention to assess the scale of the settlement attempts. The mission's findings showed that these districts had as of 2005 an overall population of 14,000 persons, mostly living in precarious social conditions. It consisted primarily of ethnic Armenians displaced from the non-conflict zones of Azerbaijan during the war. It was noted, however, that most of them had settled in the conflict zone after having lived in Armenia for several years and some held Armenian passports and even voted in Armenian elections. A smaller segment of the settlers was originally from the towns of <a href="/wiki/Gyumri" title="Gyumri">Gyumri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spitak" title="Spitak">Spitak</a> in Armenia who had lived in temporary shelters following the devastating <a href="/wiki/1988_Armenian_earthquake" title="1988 Armenian earthquake">1988 earthquake</a> before moving to Karabakh, as well as a small number of natives of Yerevan who moved there for financial reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> A field assessment mission revisited the region in October 2010, confirming that there had not been much growth in population or change in the living conditions of the settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> The Co-Chairs of the Minsk Group who visited Nagorno-Karabakh, Kalbajar and Lachin in 2014 reported seeing signs of improvements in the infrastructure but could not observe any indications that the size of the population had changed in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By June 2015, an estimated 17,000 of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>'s once 80,000-strong Armenian population had fled the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian Civil War">civil war</a> and sought refuge in Armenia.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Babayan" title="David Babayan">David Babayan</a>, spokesperson of the Artsakh leader Bako Sahakyan, confirmed that some of those refugees had been resettled in Artsakh.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> put the number of the resettled families at 30 as of June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In December 2014, Armenian media cited local municipal authorities in stating that dozens of Syrian Armenian families had been resettled in the disputed zone, in particular in the city of <a href="/wiki/Lachin" title="Lachin">Lachin</a> and the village of <a href="/wiki/Xanl%C4%B1q" title="Xanlıq">Xanlıq</a> in <a href="/wiki/Qubadli_District" title="Qubadli District">Qubadli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Azerbaijan's Minister of Foreign Affairs <a href="/wiki/Elmar_Mammadyarov" title="Elmar Mammadyarov">Elmar Mammadyarov</a> expressed his concern over Armenia's attempts to change the demographic situation in the region and informed of his intention to raise this issue with the Minsk Group.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2019, Armenia's <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Service_(Armenia)" title="National Security Service (Armenia)">National Security Service</a> director <a href="/wiki/Artur_Vanetsyan" title="Artur Vanetsyan">Artur Vanetsyan</a> visited Nagorno-Karabakh amid public concern about <a href="/wiki/Nikol_Pashinyan" title="Nikol Pashinyan">Nikol Pashinyan</a>'s government alleged readiness to cede some of the Armenian-controlled territories as part of a peace settlement. Vanetsyan pointed out that settling Armenians and investing into infrastructural projects along the Iranian border, in the previously Azeri-populated regions outside of the former autonomous province, was "a clear message" to the international community that there would be no territorial concessions. He referred to the ongoing settlement efforts as a method of "guaranteeing security".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> Azerbaijan's Foreign Ministry reacted by qualifying Vanetsyan's statement as an "attempt to undermine the peace talks and defy the work of the mediators" and vowed to address the issue to the UN and the OSCE.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ceasefire ending the 2020 war stipulated that these territories were to be turned over to Azerbaijani control. Armenian settlers in these areas evacuated prior to the arrival of Azerbaijani forces.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> </p>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg/220px-%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg/330px-%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg/440px-%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="531"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%94%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dadivank_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dadivank Monastery">Dadivank Monastery</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg/220px-Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg/330px-Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg/440px-Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1756" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ghazanchetsots_Double_Rainbow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ghazanchetsots_Cathedral" title="Ghazanchetsots Cathedral">Ghazanchetsots Cathedral</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of the Armenian population in Artsakh is Christian and belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a> which is an <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Orthodox">Oriental Orthodox</a> Church. </p>
      <p>Certain <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christianity">Eastern Orthodox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelical" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical">Evangelical</a> denominations also exist.<sup id="cite_ref-Overview_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overview-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (June 2017)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Republic_of_Artsakh#Dubious" title="Talk:Republic of Artsakh">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> However, military authorities prohibited any Christian sect activity in Artsakh, for the reason that they would preach <a href="/wiki/Pacifism" title="Pacifism">pacifism</a> among the population.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_Armenian_monasteries_and_churches">Historic Armenian monasteries and churches</span></h4> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Yeghishe_Arakyal_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Yeghishe Arakyal Monastery">Saint Yeghishe Arakyal Monastery</a> (5th–13th centuries) commemorating St. Yeghishe, the famous evangelizer of Armenia's eastern lands. The church serves as a burial ground for the 5th century's King Vachagan II the Pious, the most well-known representative of the Arranshahik line of east Armenian monarchs. The monastery is located in the <a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a> District.</li> 
       <li>Bri Yeghtze Monastery (13th century) that centres on embedded khachkars, unique-to-Armenia stone memorials with engraved crosses. The monastery is located in the <a href="/wiki/Martuni_Province" title="Martuni Province">Martuni</a> District.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Artsakh_after_2020">In Artsakh after 2020</span></h5> 
      <ul>
       <li>The <a href="/wiki/Gandzasar_monastery" title="Gandzasar monastery">Gandzasar monastery</a> ("Գանձասար" in Armenian) is a historical monastery in Artsakh. Artsakhi government's aim is to include the Gandzasar Monastery into the directory of the UNESCO's World Heritage Sites.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Amaras_Monastery" title="Amaras Monastery">Amaras Monastery</a> (4th century) was a monastery was established by the foremost Armenian saint, St. <a href="/wiki/Gregory_the_Illuminator" title="Gregory the Illuminator">Gregory the Illuminator</a>, who baptized Armenia into the world's first Christian state in AD 301. Amaras also hosted the first school where St. <a href="/wiki/Mesrop_Mashtots" title="Mesrop Mashtots">Mesrop Mashtots</a>, the inventor of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_alphabet" title="Armenian alphabet">Armenian alphabet</a>, taught the new script to pupils in the 5th century. The Amaras Monastery's location is in the <a href="/wiki/Martuni_Province" title="Martuni Province">Martuni</a> District.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> As of November 2020, the monastery is remaining under Armenian control.<sup id="cite_ref-Nouvelles2020_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nouvelles2020-152">[152]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_St._Nerses_the_Great" title="Church of St. Nerses the Great">Church of St. Nerses the Great</a>, is located in the city of <a href="/wiki/Khojavend_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Khojavend (town)">Martuni</a>. It is dedicated to the famous <a href="/wiki/Catholicos_of_Armenia" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicos of Armenia">Armenian Catholicos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Narses" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Narses">Saint Narses</a> the Great.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Yerits_Mankants_Monastery" title="Yerits Mankants Monastery">Yerits Mankants Monastery</a> (meaning "three infants" in Armenian; 17th century) is known for hosting the seat of Artsakh's rival clergy to that of the Holy See of Gandzasar. The monastery is located in the <a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a> Province.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h5><span class="mw-headline" id="In_Azerbaijan_after_2020">In Azerbaijan after 2020</span></h5> 
      <p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Nagorno-Karabakh War">2020 Nagorno-Karabakh War</a>, Azerbaijan retook control over territories containing several important Armenian monasteries and churches, such as the monasteries of Dadivank, Tzitzernavank, Gtichavank, and the Ghazanchetsots Cathedral, as well as the churches of Kanach Zham and <a href="https://hy.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D5%8D%D5%B8%D6%82%D6%80%D5%A2_%D5%80%D5%B8%D5%BE%D5%B0%D5%A1%D5%B6%D5%B6%D5%A5%D5%BD_%D5%A5%D5%AF%D5%A5%D5%B2%D5%A5%D6%81%D5%AB_(%D5%8F%D5%B8%D5%B2)" class="extiw" title="hy:Սուրբ Հովհաննես եկեղեցի (Տող)">St. Hovhannes Church (Hadrut region)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chapple_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chapple-153">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Dadivank_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dadivank Monastery">Dadivank Monastery</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Դադիվանք</span>), also known as Khutavank (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Խութավանք</span> – Monastery on the Hill), that was built between the 9th and 13th century. It is one of the most architecturally and culturally significant monasteries in Artsakh. The western façade of Dadivank's Memorial Cathedral bears one of the most extensive Armenian lapidary (stone-inscribed) texts,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2020)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:Republic_of_Artsakh#The_term_seems_to_be_literally_adopted_from_a_foreign_language_and_doesn't_mean_the_same_in_English." title="Talk:Republic of Artsakh">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> and has one of the largest collection of medieval Armenian <a href="/wiki/Frescoes" class="mw-redirect" title="Frescoes">frescoes</a>. Dadivank is named after St. Dadi, a disciple of <a href="/wiki/Apostle_Thaddeus" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostle Thaddeus">Apostle Thaddeus</a> who preached the Holy Gospel in Artsakh in the 1st century. St. Dadi's tomb was later discovered by archaeologists in 2007. The monastery is in the <a href="/wiki/Shahumian" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahumian">Shahumian</a> District and has been placed under the protection of the Russian peacekeeping forces.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tsitsernavank_Monastery" title="Tsitsernavank Monastery">Tsitsernavank Monastery</a> (4th century) is the best-preserved example of an Armenian basilica with three naves. The monastery is located in the village of <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BCs%C3%BCl%C3%BC,_Lachin" title="Hüsülü, Lachin">Tsitsernavank</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Kashatagh_Province" title="Kashatagh Province">Kashatagh Province</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gtichavank" title="Gtichavank">Gtichavank</a> Monastery (13th century) has design features shared with the architectural style of medieval Armenia's capital city of Ani. The monastery is located in the <a href="/wiki/Hadrut_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadrut Region">Hadrut</a> District.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ghazanchetsots_Cathedral" title="Ghazanchetsots Cathedral">Ghazanchetsots Cathedral</a>, built 1868–1888 (Սուրբ Ամենափրկիչ Ղազանչեցոց Եկեղեցի – "Surb Amenap'rkich Ghazanchets'ots' Yekeghets'i" in <a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>), also known as the <i>Cathedral of Christ the Savior</i> and the <i>Shushi Cathedral</i>, is an <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian church</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Shusha" title="Shusha">Shusha</a>. It is the main cathedral and headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Apostolic_Church" title="Armenian Apostolic Church">Armenian Apostolic Church</a>'s "Diocese of Artsakh".</li> 
       <li>Just uphill from the cathedral in Shusha is the <a href="/wiki/Kanach_Zham" title="Kanach Zham">Kanach Zham</a> ('Green Church' in Armenian) built in 1847.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Katarovank" title="Katarovank">Katarovank Monastery</a> was founded in the 4th century, and is located close to the village of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6hn%C9%99_Ta%C4%9Flar" class="mw-redirect" title="Köhnə Tağlar">Hin Tagher</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hadrut_Province" title="Hadrut Province">Hadrut Province</a>. The present-day chapel is a 17th-century structure. There are Armenian <a href="/wiki/Khachkars" class="mw-redirect" title="Khachkars">khachkars</a> near the chapel. The monastery offers a unique panoramic view to the <a href="/wiki/River_Araxes" class="mw-redirect" title="River Araxes">River Araxes</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Republic_of_Artsakh" title="Economy of the Republic of Artsakh">Economy of the Republic of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg/220px-Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg/330px-Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg/440px-Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1160" data-file-height="870"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_downtown_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A hotel in downtown Stepanakert
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The socio-economic situation of the Republic of Artsakh was greatly affected by the 1991–1994 conflict. Yet, foreign investments began to come. The origin of most venture capital comes from Armenians in Armenia, Russia, United States, France, Australia, Iran, and the Middle East. </p>
      <p>Notably the telecommunications sector was developed with Karabakh Telecom<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> investing millions of dollars in mobile telephony, spearheaded by a Lebanese company. </p>
      <p>Copper and gold mining has been advancing since 2002 with development and launch of operations at <a href="/wiki/Drmbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Drmbon">Drmbon</a> deposit.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Approximately 27–28 thousand tons (wet weight) of concentrates are produced<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> with average copper content of 19–21% and gold content of 32–34 g/t.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> Azerbaijan considers any mining operations in Nagorno-Karabakh illegal and has vowed to engage an international audit company to determine the damages suffered by Azerbaijan's state-run ore management company as a result. In 2018, the government of Azerbaijan announced that it was planning to appeal to an international court and the law enforcement agencies of the countries where the mining companies involved are registered.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The banking system is administered by <a href="/wiki/Artsakhbank" title="Artsakhbank">Artsakhbank</a> (a Yerevan-based Armenian bank fulfilling the functions of the state bank of Nagorno-Karabakh) and a number of other Armenian banks. The republic uses the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_dram" title="Armenian dram">Armenian dram</a>. </p>
      <p>Wine growing and processing of agricultural products, particularly wine (i.e., storage of wine, wine stuffs, cognac alcohol) is one of the prioritized directions of the economic development.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karmir-shuka.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Karmir-shuka.jpeg/220px-Karmir-shuka.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Karmir-shuka.jpeg/330px-Karmir-shuka.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Karmir-shuka.jpeg/440px-Karmir-shuka.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karmir-shuka.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Karmir_Shuka" class="mw-redirect" title="Karmir Shuka">Karmir Shuka</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Prior to the 2020 war, the republic developed a tourist industry geared to Armenia and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>. The republic showed a major increase in tourists over the last several years because of Artsakh's many cultural sights. Before the 2020 war there were nine<sup id="cite_ref-Solutions_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solutions-161">[161]</a></sup> hotels in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. The Artsakh development agency says 4,000 tourists visited Artsakh in 2005. The figures rose to 8,000 in 2010 (excluding visitors from Armenia).<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The agency cooperated with the Armenia Tourism Development Agency (ATDA) as Armenia is the only way tourists (mainly Armenians) can access Artsakh. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Artsakh reported continuous expansion of visitors' geography.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Tourist infrastructure was developed around sites such as monasteries that showcase the Armenian history in the region,<sup id="cite_ref-Toal_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toal-16">[16]</a></sup> with Islamic sites rarely restored,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> while some ghost cities and areas near the front line were off limit to tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-Toal_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toal-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Tourism Development Agency of Artsakh was established in Yerevan as a non-governmental organisation in the Republic of Armenia to promote tourism further in Artsakh. It makes preparations for tour operators, travel agencies and journalists covering the region, and arranges for hotel services, shopping, catering, recreation centers. </p>
      <p>Tourist attractions included: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gandzasar_monastery" title="Gandzasar monastery">Gandzasar monastery</a>, main tourist attraction.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ghazanchetsots_Cathedral" title="Ghazanchetsots Cathedral">Ghazanchetsots Cathedral</a> of the Holy Savior.</li> 
       <li>Church of the Holy Mother of God "<a href="/wiki/Kanach_Zham" title="Kanach Zham">Kanach Zham</a>".</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Amaras_Monastery" title="Amaras Monastery">Amaras Monastery</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tsitsernavank_Monastery" title="Tsitsernavank Monastery">Tsitsernavank Monastery</a>.</li> 
       <li>St. <a href="/wiki/Yeghishe_Arakyal_Monastery" title="Yeghishe Arakyal Monastery">Yeghishe Arakyal Monastery</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Dadivank_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dadivank Monastery">Dadivank Monastery</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gtichavank_monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Gtichavank monastery">Gtichavank monastery</a>.</li> 
       <li>Bri Yeghtsi monastery.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Yeritsmankants_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Yeritsmankants Monastery">Yerits Mankants</a>.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Katarovank_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Katarovank Monastery">Katarovank Monastery</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Other tourist attractions included: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Fort Mayraberd (10th–18th centuries) served as the primary bulwark against Turko-nomadic incursions from the eastern steppe. The fort is found to the east of the region's capital city of <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>.</li> 
       <li>Govharagha Mosque (18th century), a mosque located in the city of Shusha, now under Azerbaijani control.</li>
      </ul> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG/220px-Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG/330px-Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG/440px-Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Karintak-IMG_1445.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Section of <a href="/wiki/Janapar" title="Janapar">Janapar</a> trail.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Janapar" title="Janapar">Janapar</a> Trail is a marked trail, through mountains, valleys, and villages of Artsakh, with monasteries and fortresses along the way.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> It's not hikable since the 2020 Nagorno-Karabakh war. The trail was broken into day hikes, which brought tourists to a different village each night.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The paths have existed for centuries but now are marked specifically for hikers. The Himnakan Janapar (backbone trail), marked in 2007, leads from the northwest region of <a href="/wiki/Shahumian" class="mw-redirect" title="Shahumian">Shahumian</a> to the southern town of <a href="/wiki/Hadrut_(town)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadrut (town)">Hadrut</a>, now under Azerbaijani control. Side trails and mini trails take one to additional parts of Artsakh. The important sites passed along this hike include <a href="/wiki/Dadivank_Monastery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dadivank Monastery">Dadivank Monastery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gandzasar_monastery" title="Gandzasar monastery">Gandzasar monastery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shusha" title="Shusha">Shusha</a>, the Karkar Canyon with its high cliffs, Zontik Waterfall, and the ruins of Hunot and <a href="/wiki/Gtichavank" title="Gtichavank">Gtichavank</a> monastery. </p>
      <p>One of the noteworthy side trails is the Gtichavank Loop Trail. This loop starts from <a href="/wiki/Tugh" class="mw-redirect" title="Tugh">Tugh</a> Village, now under Azerbaijani control. </p>
      <p>The cost of staying in Artsakh is relatively cheap in comparison with the rest of the region and varies approximately between 25 – US$70 for a single person as of May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Solutions_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solutions-161">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, those who travelled to Artsakh without the Azerbaijani government's prior consent and permission will be denied entry to Azerbaijan since the country considers Artsakh their territory unlawfully occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Armenia" title="Armed Forces of Armenia">Armenian army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The Azerbaijani government also keeps and publishes online a list of foreign nationals who visited these occupied areas without prior approval.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> In late 2017, the list contained 699 names with additional details (date, country, profession, purpose of visit). The earliest entry recorded a visit to Artsakh that occurred on an unspecified date sometime between 1993 and 1996. The list includes many journalists and members of parliaments of foreign countries. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Artsakh_Wine_Fest">Artsakh Wine Fest</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_Wine_Fest" title="Artsakh Wine Fest">Artsakh Wine Fest</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Artcraft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Artcraft.jpg/220px-Artcraft.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Artcraft.jpg/330px-Artcraft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Artcraft.jpg/440px-Artcraft.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Artcraft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Exhibition of artworks at Artsakh Wine Fest
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before the 2020 war, the <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_Wine_Fest" title="Artsakh Wine Fest">Artsakh Wine Fest</a> took place annually in <a href="/wiki/Togh" class="mw-redirect" title="Togh">Togh</a> since 2014. The festival was held on the third Saturday of each September.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The festival was initiated by the Department of Tourism and Protection of Historical Places of the Ministry of Culture, Tourism and Youth Affairs of the Republic of Artsakh and was aimed to develop tourism in Artsakh.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> It was meant to restore Artsakh <a href="/wiki/Winemaking" title="Winemaking">winemaking</a> traditions. The festival provided a platform to the winemakers of Artsakh and Armenia giving them an opportunity to sell their products, exchange knowledge, promote their wine etc. The annual festival's program included grape stomping, tasting of traditional Artsakh cuisine, an exhibition of artworks, an exhibition of ancient artefacts that belonged to the Melik Yegan's Palace, as well as an exhibition and sale of local wine, where one could find products from 5 different regions of Artsakh and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a>. Traditionally, the festival was accompanied by Armenian national singing and dancing. The festival evolved into a national holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG/220px-Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG/330px-Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG/440px-Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stepanakert_Airport_Daytime.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stepanakert_Airport" title="Stepanakert Airport">Stepanakert Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The transportation system had been damaged by the 1991–1994 conflict, but was noticeably improved before the 2020 war:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (March 2019)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the North–South Artsakh motorway alone largely facilitated the development of the transportation system.<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia_Fund_USA_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia_Fund_USA-172">[172]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before the 2020 war, the 169-kilometre (105&nbsp;mi) Hadrut-Stepanakert-Askeran-Martakert motorway, the locals said, was the lifeline of Artsakh, and $25 million donated during the Hayastan All-Armenian Foundation telethons was allotted for the construction of the road.<sup id="cite_ref-Armenia_Fund_USA_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Armenia_Fund_USA-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert_Airport" title="Stepanakert Airport">Stepanakert Airport</a>, the sole civilian airport of the Republic of Artsakh, located about 8 kilometres (5 miles) east of the capital, has been closed since the onset of the war in 1990. However, the government was pressing ahead with plans to reopen the airport as of early 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Republic_of_Artsakh&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and raised about 1 billion drams ($2.8 million) for its reconstruction from unspecified "charitable sources". It began building a new airport terminal and repairing the runway in late 2009. In any case, its unresolved status makes direct air communication with other countries all but impossible according to IATA conventions.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Though originally scheduled to launch the first commercial flights on 9 May 2011, Artsakh officials postponed a new reopening date throughout the whole of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> In May 2012, the director of the Artsakh Civil Aviation Administration, Tigran Gabrielyan, announced that the airport would begin operations in mid-2012.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> However the airport still remains closed due to security reasons, as Azerbaijan has threatened to shoot down planes using the airport. </p>
      <p>A new route from the Armenian capital <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a> to Stepanakert was planned to bypass the 8–9 hours drive via the Lachin corridor.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> It was opened in September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> A third road was planned in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Following the 2020 war, a new road will be built along the Lachin corridor to bypass Shusha.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Authorities in the USSR opened a railway line in the Nagorno-Karabakh Autonomous Oblast in 1944. It line connected the capital, Stepanakert, and <a href="/wiki/Yevlax" class="mw-redirect" title="Yevlax">Yevlax</a> in Azerbaijan. It was built to Russian standard gauge of 1520mm. Due to the first Nagorno-Karabakh War, the line the railway was badly damaged and the line was closed.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_(03).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg/220px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg/330px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg/440px-2014_Stepanakert%2C_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_%2803%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4656" data-file-height="3104"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2014_Stepanakert,_Pa%C5%84stwowy_Uniwersytet_Arcachu_(03).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Artsakh_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Artsakh State University">Artsakh State University</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Artsakh is compulsory, and is free up to the age of 18. The education system is inherited from the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Education in the Soviet Union">old system</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Artsakh's school system was severely damaged because of the 1991–1994 conflict. But the government of the Republic of Artsakh with considerable aid from the Republic of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> and with donations from the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>, rebuilt many of the schools. Prior to the 2020 war, Artsakh had around 250 schools of various sizes, with more than 200 lying in the regions. The student population was estimated at more than 20,000, with almost half in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Artsakh_State_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Artsakh State University">Artsakh State University</a> was founded by Artsakh and Armenian governments' joint efforts, with main campus in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. The university opening ceremony took place on 10 May 1992. </p>
      <p>Yerevan University of Management also opened a branch in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Artsakh" title="Culture of Artsakh">Culture of Artsakh</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tatikpapik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tatikpapik.jpg/220px-Tatikpapik.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tatikpapik.jpg/330px-Tatikpapik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Tatikpapik.jpg/440px-Tatikpapik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tatikpapik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>We Are Our Mountains</i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>"<a href="/wiki/We_Are_Our_Mountains" title="We Are Our Mountains">We Are Our Mountains</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Armenian_language" title="Armenian language">Armenian</a>: <span lang="hy">Մենք ենք մեր սարերը</span>) by <a href="/wiki/Sargis_Baghdasaryan" title="Sargis Baghdasaryan">Sargis Baghdasaryan</a> is a monument located in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> The sculpture is widely regarded as a symbol of the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> independent Republic of Artsakh. It is a large monument from <a href="/wiki/Tuff" title="Tuff">tuff</a> of an old Armenian man and woman hewn from rock, representing the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain people">mountain people</a> of Artsakh. It is also known as <i>Tatik yev Papik</i> (Տատիկ և Պապիկ) in Armenian. The sculpture is featured prominently on <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Nagorno-Karabakh" class="mw-redirect" title="Coat of arms of Nagorno-Karabakh">Artsakh's coat of arms</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_State_Museum_(37512504202).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg/220px-Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg/330px-Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg/440px-Artsakh_State_Museum_%2837512504202%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Artsakh_State_Museum_(37512504202).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Artsakh State Museum
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Artsakh_State_Museum" title="Artsakh State Museum">Artsakh State Museum</a> is the historical museum of the Republic of Artsakh. Located at 4 Sasunstsi David Street, in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>, the museum offers an assortment of ancient artifacts and Christian manuscripts. There are also more recent items, ranging in date from the 19th century to World War II and from events of the Karabakh Independence War. </p>
      <p>Artsakh has its own brand of popular music. As Artsakh question became a pan-Armenian question, Artsakh music was further promoted worldwide. </p>
      <p>Many nationalist songs, performed by Artsakhi artists, as well as artists from Republic of <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_diaspora" title="Armenian diaspora">Armenian diaspora</a>, show support for the Artsakh independence movement; videos for the songs, incorporate footage of Artsakhi military campaigns. These videos are posted to sites such as YouTube, where they often generate conflicting nationalist Armenian and Azerbaijani comments. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Publications">Publications</span></h3> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Azat_Artsakh" title="Azat Artsakh">Azat Artsakh</a></i> is the official newspaper of the Republic of Artsakh. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stepenakert_view_no.2,_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg/220px-Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg/330px-Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg/440px-Stepenakert_view_no.2%2C_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2944" data-file-height="1588"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stepenakert_view_no.2,_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Stepanakert_Republican_Stadium" title="Stepanakert Republican Stadium">Stepanakert Republican Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Sports in the Republic of Artsakh are organised by the Artsakh Ministry of Culture and Youth. Due to the non-recognition of Artsakh, sports teams from the country cannot compete in most international tournaments. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Artsakh. <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a> has a well-built football stadium. Since the mid-1990s, football teams from Artsakh started taking part in some domestic competitions in Armenia. <a href="/wiki/Lernayin_Artsakh_FC" title="Lernayin Artsakh FC">Lernayin Artsakh FC</a> represents the city of <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a>. In Artsakh, domestic football clubs play in the <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_Football_League" title="Artsakh Football League">Artsakh Football League</a>. The Artsakh football league was launched in 2009. The <a href="/wiki/Artsakh_national_football_team" title="Artsakh national football team">Artsakh national football team</a> was formed in 2012 and played their first competitive match against the <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia_national_football_team" title="Abkhazia national football team">Abkhazia national football team</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sokhumi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sokhumi">Sokhumi</a>, a match that ended with a result of 1–1 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> The return match between the unrecognized teams took place at the <a href="/wiki/Stepanakert" title="Stepanakert">Stepanakert</a> Stadium, on 21 October 2012, when the team from Artsakh defeated the Abkhazian team 3–0. </p>
      <p>There is also interest in other sports, including basketball and volleyball. Sailing is practised in the town of <a href="/wiki/Martakert" title="Martakert">Martakert</a>. </p>
      <p>Artsakh sports teams and athletes also participate in the <a href="/wiki/Pan-Armenian_Games" title="Pan-Armenian Games">Pan-Armenian Games</a> organised in Armenia. </p>

       <li><a href="/wiki/Armenian-occupied_territories_surrounding_Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Armenian-occupied territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh">Armenian-occupied territories surrounding Nagorno-Karabakh</a></li>

           <div id="Movements_of_regionalism,_separatism_and_stateless_nationalism_in_Europe" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">

           </div></th>
